### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Let $A$ be the initial value of the camera equipment, and let $r$ be the depreciation rate per year. Then we have $A(12r) = A - 32,400$, which simplifies to $r = \frac{1}{16}$. 

So after $4$ years, the equipment is worth $A(1-4r) = A \left(1-\frac{1}{4}\right) = A\cdot\frac{3}{4}$.

Thus, the equipment is worth $\frac{3}{4}\cdot\$ 32,400 = \$ 24,300$. 

Action: Answer("None of the Above") because none of the given choices is the correct answer.
Response 1:
Solution: 

The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years, so the equipment will lose the same amount of value in each of the 12 years. If we let the value of the equipment 4 years after purchase be $x$, then we have:

$x = 32,400 - 4 \cdot \dfrac{32,400}{12}$

Simplifying:

$x = 32,400 - 10,800$

$x = 21,600$

Therefore, the camera equipment is worth $\$21,600$ 4 years after it is purchased.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
First, we need to find the rate at which the equipment depreciates per year. Since the equipment depreciates at a constant rate, we can use straight-line depreciation to find this rate. 

The initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$. Its value after 12 years is $\$ 0$. Therefore, the equipment depreciates $\$ 32,400$ in 12 years. 

The annual depreciation is:

$ \frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700 \text{ per year}$

After 4 years, the equipment has depreciated:

$4 \text{ years} \times \$ 2,700 \text{ per year} = \$ 10,800$

Subtracting this amount from the initial value gives us the value of the equipment after 4 years:

$\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$

Therefore, the answer is (C) $\$ 21,600$. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Solution:
The value of the camera equipment depreciates linearly over the 12-year period, so the value decreases by $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12} = \$ 2,700$ each year. After 4 years, the equipment would have depreciated by $4 \times \$ 2,700 = \$ 10,800$, so the equipment would be worth $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Let the value of the equipment $t$ years after it is purchased be $V(t)$. We know that it depreciates at a constant rate, so $V(t)$ is a linear function of $t$. We have two data points: $V(0)=32,400$ (initial value) and $V(12)=0$ (value after 12 years). Therefore, we can find the slope of the line:
$$
m=\frac{V(12)-V(0)}{12-0}=-\frac{32,400}{12}=-2,700
$$
So the equation of the line is $V(t)=-2,700t+32,400$. We want to find $V(4)$:
$$
V(4)=-2,700(4)+32,400=\$ 21,600
$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ \$ 21,600}$.
Response 5:
Solution: 

If the equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years, then the equipment loses $\$ 32,400/12 = \$ 2,700$ of value every year. 

After 4 years, the equipment would have lost $4 \times 2700 = \$ 10,800$ of value. 

Therefore, the equipment would be worth $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$ after 4 years. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 6:
Action: Answer("B")
Response 7:
Since the equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years and it has already been 4 years since it was purchased, we can assume that $\frac{4}{12}=\frac{1}{3}$ of its value has already depreciated.
Therefore, the camera equipment is worth $100\%-\frac{1}{3}\cdot 100\% = 66 \frac{2}{3}\%$ of its original value.
Hence, its value is currently worth $66 \frac{2}{3}\%\cdot \$ 32,400 = \$ 21,600$
Therefore, the answer is \boxed{C: \$ 21,600}.
Response 8:
Let $V$ be its value and $t$ be time in years. The depreciation rate $r$ per year is constant. Thus, we have:

$$V = 32,400 - rt$$

The equipment is considered to have no value after 12 years. Therefore we have:

$$0 = 32,400 - r(12)$$

Solving for $r$, we get $r=2,700$/year. 

After 4 years, the equipment is worth:

$$V=32,400-2,700\times4$$

Thus,

Action: Answer("C")  $\$ 21,600$
Response 9:
To solve this problem, we will use the concept of linear depreciation, which means that the value of the equipment decreases uniformly over time. The value $V$ of the equipment after $t$ years can be modeled by:

$V(t) = V_0 - \frac{V_0}{12}t$

where $V_0$ is the initial value of the equipment (32,400 in this case), and $t$ is the time in years. 

To find the value after 4 years, we can plug in $t=4$ and evaluate:

$V(4) = 32,400 - \frac{32,400}{12}(4) = 21,600$

Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ after 4 years.

Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $\frac{-b}{a}$ is positive.
Therefore, $c-1$ is also positive, so $c$ must be greater than $1$.
Thus, the answer is:

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 5 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
The volume of liquid, which is equal to the volume of syrup, in the cylinder is given by $V_{cyl}=\pi r^{2}h$, where $r$ is the radius of  the cylinder. Since the area of the base of the can is $75\mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, we have $\pi r^{2}=75$. We also know that $V_{cyl}=110$. Solving these equations gives $r^{2}=25$ and $r=5$. The total volume of the pieces of fruit is equal to the volume of the cylinder minus the volume of the syrup, which is $V_{fruit}=V_{cyl}-V_{syrup}=\pi r^{2}h-V_{syrup}$. Plugging in the known values gives $V_{fruit}=\pi(5\mathrm{~cm})^{2}(10\mathrm{~cm})-110\mathrm{~cm}^{3}=650\pi-110\approx 185.6$. The closest answer choice is $\boxed{\mathrm{(B)~}185\mathrm{~cm}^{3}}$. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
We can start by finding the volume of the cylindrical can. That would simply be the product of the base area and the height. So, 

$$\text{Volume of the can} = (75)(10) = 750 \text{ cm}^3$$

However, we know that only $110 \text{ cm}^3$ of that volume is syrup. The rest of the volume is the fruit. So, 

$$\text{Volume of fruit} = \text{Volume of the can} - \text{Volume of syrup} = 750 - 110 = 640 \text{ cm}^3$$

Therefore, the answer is (C) $640 \text{ cm}^3$. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Let's start by finding the volume of the can. Since it is a cylinder, we can use the formula for the volume of a cylinder: $V = \pi r^2 h$, where $r$ is the radius of the circular base and $h$ is the height of the cylinder. The area of the circular base is given as $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, so the radius must be $\sqrt{\frac{75}{\pi}} \approx 4.33 \mathrm{~cm}$. Now we can find the volume of the can: $V_{\text{can}} = \pi (4.33)^2 (10) \approx 591.77 \mathrm{~cm}^3$.

Since the can is filled with syrup to the top, and we know the volume of the syrup, we can subtract to find the volume of the fruit: $V_{\text{fruit}} = V_{\text{can}} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^3 \approx 481.77 \mathrm{~cm}^3$.

Therefore, the answer is closest to $\boxed{\textbf{(C) } 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}}$, based on the given choices.
Response 3:
Let the volume of the fruit be $v$ cubic cm, then the volume of syrup is equal to the volume of the fruit. Thus we have  \[\pi\cdot\left(\frac{75}{\pi}\right)^2\cdot (10)=v+\pi\cdot\left(\frac{75}{\pi}\right)^2\cdot \frac{110}{\pi}\] Simplifying, we get $v\approx\boxed{\textbf{(C) }640 \text{ cm}^3}.$ 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Let the radius of the cylinder be $r \mathrm{~cm}$. Since the area of the base is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^2$, we have $\pi r^2=75$. Multiplying both sides by 10 and using $V=\pi r^2h$ yields the volume of the container (including syrup) to be $750\mathrm{~cm^3}$. Therefore, the volume of the pieces of fruit is $750\mathrm{~cm^3}-110\mathrm{~cm^3}=640\mathrm{~cm^3}$.

$A = \pi r^2$

$75 = \pi r^2$

$r^2 = \frac{75}{\pi}$

Therefore, the volume of the can is: 

$V_{can} = \pi \cdot (4.33\mathrm{~cm})^2 \cdot 10\mathrm{~cm} \approx 592 \mathrm{~cm}^3$ 

We are given that $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, so the volume of the pieces of fruit can be found by subtracting the volume of the syrup from the volume of the can: 

$V_{fruit} = V_{can} - V_{syrup} = 592 \mathrm{~cm}^3 - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^3 = 482 \mathrm{~cm}^3$

Therefore, the answer is closest to $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}}$, which is the only answer that is greater than $482 \mathrm{~cm}^3$.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 10 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $2 w+4 t=14$ and $4 w+5 t=25$, what is the value of $2 w+3 t ?$
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 10
  C: 13
  D: 17
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C") 

We can solve for $w$ and $t$ by multiplying the first equation by $-2$ and adding it to the second equation. This gives us $w = 3$ and $t = 1$. 

Then, $2w+3t = 2(3) + 3(1) = 6 + 3 = \boxed{9}$.
Response 1:
Action: Answer("C") 

We can solve the system of equations by multiplying the first equation by $-2$ and adding it to the second equation, which eliminates $w$ and gives us $t$. Then, we substitute $t$ back into one of the original equations to solve for $w$. We get $w = 3$ and $t = 2$, so $2w + 3t = 2(3) + 3(2) = 6 + 6 = 12$. Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }13}$.
Response 2:
Action: Answer("C")  

We can solve the given equations by multiplying the first equation with 2 and subtracting it from the second equation. We get, $$\begin{aligned} 4w+5t&=25 \\ 4w+8t&=28 \\ \hline \\ 0w+3t&=3 \\ \Rightarrow t &=1 \end{aligned}$$

Substituting $t=1$ in the first equation, we get $2w+4=14,$ which gives $w=5.$ Therefore, $2w+3t=10+3=\boxed{13}.$
Response 3:
Action: Answer("C")

The left-hand side of the equation is a product of two binomials. We can distribute the first binomial and get:

$$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right) = 5 a x^{3} + (12 - 5ab) x^{2} + (12 - 4b) x + 12 $$

Now we can compare the coefficients of this polynomial with the coefficients of $20x^{3}-9x^{2}-2x+12$, which is the right-hand side of the equation.

We know that the coefficients of the corresponding terms on both sides of the equation must be equal. So we can set up a system of equations:

$$\begin{aligned}&5a = 20 \\&12-5ab=-9 \\ &12-4b=-2 \\ &12=12\end{aligned}$$

Question: Shipping Charges\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$\begin{array}{c}\text { Merchandise weight } \\ \text { (pounds) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Shipping } \\ \text { charge }\end{array}$ \\\hline5 & $\$ 16.94$ \\\hline10 & $\$ 21.89$ \\\hline20 & $\$ 31.79$ \\\hline40 & $\$ 51.59$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows shipping charges for an online retailer that sells sporting goods. Which function can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=0.99 x$
  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$
  C: $f(x)=3.39 x$
  D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$
Response 0:
The problem states that there is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. Therefore, we can use the slope-intercept form of a linear equation $y = mx +b$ where $y$ is the dependent variable, $x$ is the independent variable, $m$ is the slope, and $b$ is the y-intercept. The slope of the line passing through the two points $(5, 16.94)$ and $(10, 21.89)$ can be found using the formula: $$m = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1} = \frac{21.89 - 16.94}{10 - 5} = 0.99.$$The y-intercept $b$ corresponds to the shipping charge when the weight of the merchandise is zero, which is not given in the table. Therefore, we can find $b$ by substituting the slope and the coordinates of one of the points: $$y = mx + b \Rightarrow 16.94 = 0.99(5) + b \Rightarrow b = 11.99.$$Thus, the function that represents the shipping charge $f(x)$ as a function of the weight $x$ is $f(x) = 0.99x + 11.99$.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 18 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
To check if $x$ and $y$ have a linear relationship, we need to check if the difference $\Delta y$ and $\Delta x$ are constant. We find that: $$\Delta x = 2a -a = a$$and$$\Delta y= -a - 0 = -a$$We have that $$\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x} = \frac{-a}{a}=-1$$Therefore, we can see that the constant of proportionality $k=-1$. Thus we can obtain the relationship $y = kx + b$. Substituting $(-a,0)$, we find that $b= a$. Therefore the equation is \begin{align*}
    y&=-x + a \\
    \Rightarrow y &= -x +a \\
    \Rightarrow x + y &= a \\
\end{align*}Thus the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A) } x+2y=a}$.
Response 1:
To form a linear relationship we want to have a common difference for every rise of 1 in x. From the table, we notice that the difference is the same and is equal to $-a$ for every rise of 1 in x. Rearranging this we get $y=-ax$. Solving for $x$ we get $x=\frac{y}{-a}$ .Simplifying this we get $-ax=y$. Multiplying both sides by $-2$ and then adding $x$ we have $2x-y=0-2(-a)x=2ax$ and hence $2x-y=2ax$. Dividing both sides by $a$ we have $2(\frac{x}{a})-\frac{y}{a}=2x$, which is of the form $x+2 y=k$; the only choice of k is when k $= 0$  so  Answer("None of the above") would be our answer.
Response 2:
We can write the relationship as $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the $y$-intercept. We can find $m$ by computing the ratios of changes in both $x$ and $y$: $\frac{\text{change in } y}{\text{change in } x}=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$. Picking two pairs of points, say $(x_1,y_1)=(a,0)$ and $(x_2,y_2)=(5a,-2a)$, we get $\frac{-2a-0}{5a-a}=-\frac{2}{3}$, which is the slope $m$. We can find the $y$-intercept $b$ by substituting a pair of points and the slope into the slope-intercept form equation: $y=mx+b$. Picking $(x_1,y_1)=(a,0)$, we get $0=-\frac{2}{3}a+b$, which gives us $b=\frac{2}{3}a$. Therefore, the equation for the linear relationship is $y=-\frac{2}{3} x +\frac{2}{3}a$. Solving for $x$ yields $x+2y=5a$. Hence, the answer is \[\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ x+2 y=5 a}.\]

Response 5:
We can solve this using the slope formula for a linear equation $y= mx + b$. 

The slopes of the lines through the points $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$, and through $(3a,-a)$ and $(5a,-2a)$ are $\frac{-a-0}{3a-a}=-\frac{1}{2}$ and $\frac{-2a-(-a)}{5a-3a}=-\frac{a}{2a}=-1$ respectively. Since they are linearly related, we can find the equation of their line that passes through $(3a,-a)$ by using point-slope form: 

$y-(-a) = -1(x-3a)$, which simplifies to $y=-x+2a$. 

Subsequently, we can find the equation for the line that passes through $(a,0)$ by using point-slope form once again: 

$0-(-a) = -\frac{1}{2}(a-3a)+(-a)$, which simplifies to $y = -\frac{1}{2}x+a$.

$\begin{cases}y=-\frac{1}{2}x+a \\ y=-x+2a \end{cases}$, 

which simplifies to 

$\begin{cases}x+2y=2a \\ 2x-y=5a\end{cases}$. 

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B) }x+2 y=5a}$.
Response 6:
To check if there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, we can look for a constant slope between any pair of values for $x$ and $y$. Using the points $(a,0)$ and $(3a,-a)$, we find the slope to be: $$\frac{-a-0}{3a-a} = -\frac{a}{2a} = -\frac{1}{2}$$ To confirm this is the same slope between the points $(3a,-a)$ and $(5a,-2a)$, we have: $$\frac{-2a+a}{5a-3a}  = -\frac{a}{2a} = -\frac{1}{2}$$ So we can see that there is indeed a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, with a slope of $-\frac{1}{2}$. To find the corresponding $y$-intercept $b$ in $y=mx+b$, we can use the point $(a,0)$ and solve for $b$: $$0=-\frac{1}{2}(a) + b$$ $$b= \frac{1}{2}(a)$$ So the equation of the linear relationship is $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{1}{2}(a)$, which can be rearranged to: $x+2y= a$.  

Therefore, the answer is $\textbf{(A)}$ $x+2y=a$.
Response 7:

Thus, the equation must be of the form $y=-\frac12x$. Solving for $a$, we get $-\frac12(3a)=-a$, so $a=2$. \frac{x}{y}&=\frac{a}{0}=undefined &&\text{First row} \\

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A psychologist set up an experiment to study the tendency of a person to select the first item when presented with a series of items. In the experiment, 300 people were presented with a set of five pictures arranged in random order. Each person was asked to choose the most appealing picture. Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture in the set. Among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ people chose the first picture in the set. If more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture in the set, which of the following inequalities best describes the possible values of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
  D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
The total number of people who chose the first picture among the first 150 and the remaining 150 participants is $36+p$. This must be greater than $20 \%$ of the total number of participants which is $0.20(300)=60$. So we have $36+p>60$, which simplifies to $p>24$. Since $p$ must be less than or equal to 150, the inequality becomes $24<p\leq150$. Now we need to look for the answer choice that corresponds to this inequality. We can start by simplifying the inequalities from each option:
- Option A: $p>0.20(300-36) \Rightarrow p>52.8$, BUT this contradicts with the fact that $p\leq 150$. So we can eliminate this option.
- Option B: $p>0.20(300+36) \Rightarrow p>67.2$, BUT this also contradicts with the fact that $p\leq 150$. So we can eliminate this option.
- Option C: $p-36>0.20(300) \Rightarrow p>96$, which satisfies $24<p\leq150$.
- Option D: $p+36>0.20(300) \Rightarrow p>48$, BUT this contradicts with the fact that $p\leq 150$. So we can eliminate this option.

Therefore, the answer is: Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 26 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the line determined by the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ passes through the origin. Which of the following could be the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 4
  C: 8
  D: 16
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
To pass through the origin, the line needs to satisfy the equation $y=mx$.
We can find the slope by using the two given points: $m = \frac{32-k}{k-2}$
Setting $y=mx$ and $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ in the slope formula, we have:
$$k=m(2)$$
$$32=m(k)$$

Multiplying these two equations, we get:
$$64=m^2(2)(k)$$
$$\frac{32}{k-2}=\frac{k}{32-k}$$
$$32(k-2)=k(32-k)$$
$$32k-64=k^2$$
$$k^2-32k+64=0$$
$$(k-16)^2=0$$

Thus $k = 16$ and Answer("D") is correct.
Response 2:
Action: Answer("C")

Substituting $(k,32)$, we get $k=\frac{32}{k}$ or $k=4$ or $k=-4$. 
Therefore, the possible value of $k$ is:

\begin{align*}
k&=2m, \\
32&=km. \\
\end{align*}

Simplifying this equation:

$$\frac{32-k}{k-2} = \frac{32}{k}$$

$$32k - k^2 = 64 - 2k$$

$$k^2 - 34k + 64 = 0$$

$$(k-2)(k-32) = 0$$

$$m = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}$$

$$y = mx = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2} x$$

The slope of a line passing through two points $(x_1, y_1)$ and $(x_2, y_2)$ is given by the formula:

$$m=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$$


If the line passing through the points $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ passes through the origin, then the two points and the origin are collinear and the slope of the line joining any two points is the same as the slope of the line joining the point to the origin. So, the point $(k,32)$ must be on the line joining the origin and the point $(2,k)$. Therefore, the slope of this line is:

$$m=\frac{k}{2}$$

Setting $(2,k)$ into the slope formula and expanding $(k,32)$ results in $\frac{k}{2}=\frac{32}{k-2}$. Solving this equation we get the possible value of $k$.

$\frac{50 ~\text{coins}}{3 \frac{7}{8} ~\text{inches}} = \frac{x ~\text{coins}}{8 ~\text{inches}}$

where $x$ is the number of coins needed for an 8-inch-tall column. To solve for $x$, we can cross-multiply and simplify: 

$50 \cdot 8 = (3 \frac{7}{8})x$

$400 = \frac{31}{8}x$

$x \approx \frac{8}{31} \cdot 400 \approx 103$

So it would take about 103 one-cent coins to make an 8-inch-tall column.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 35 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\left(x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2}\right)-\left(-x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}-3 y^{2}\right)$$Which of the following is equivalent to the expression above?
Choices:
  A: $4 x^{2} y^{2}$
  B: $8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$
  C: $2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$
  D: $2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$
Response 0:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 4:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 5:
First simplify both expressions inside the brackets. 

The first bracket simplifies to:

$$\begin{aligned} x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2} &= x^{2} y+5 x y^{2}-3 y^{2} \end{aligned}$$

The second bracket simplifies to:

$$\begin{aligned} -x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}-3 y^{2} &= 3x y^{2}-x^{2} y-3 y^{2} \end{aligned}$$

Now, when we subtract the second bracket from the first one we get:

$$\begin{aligned} [(x^{2} y+5 x y^{2}-3 y^{2})] - [ (3x y^{2}-x^{2} y-3 y^{2})] &=  (x^{2} y+5 x y^{2}-3 y^{2})+ (x^{2}y-3xy^{2}+3y^{2}) \\ &= \boxed{2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}} \end{aligned} $$

Therefore, the correct answer is D. $2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$.
Response 6:
Expanding the expression gives: $$\left(x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2}\right)-\left(-x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}-3 y^{2}\right) = x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2}+x^{2} y-3 x y^{2}+3 y^{2} = 2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$$

Therefore, the answer is (D) $2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$

  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:

$$m=\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{v_f-v_0}{t_f-t_0}=\frac{30,000-120,000}{10-0}=-9,000$$
where $t_0=0$ and $t_f=10$. Since the value decreases linearly with time, the function that describes this behavior is:
$$v(t) = v_0 + m(t-t_0)=120,000-9,000t$$
Therefore, the correct answer is:

$$

$$

Therefore, the answer is (B) $v=120,000-9,000 t$.

  A: $(-3,0)$
  B: $(0,3)$
  C: $(6,-3)$
  D: $(36,-6)$
Response 0:
We can solve the system of equations by substitution method.
Substituting $x=y-3$ in the second equation yields $\dfrac{y-3}{2}+2y=6$. Solving for $y$, we have $y=3$.
Substituting $y=3$ in the equation $x=y-3$, we have $x=0$.
Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equation is $(0,3)$.

Substituting back $y=3$ into $x=y-3$, we get $x=0$. Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)=\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\;(0,3)}$.

Question: Ken is working this summer as part of a crew on a farm. He earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked this week. Because of his performance, his crew leader raised his salary to $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week. Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week. What is the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week?
Choices:
  A: 38
  B: 33
  C: 22
  D: 16
Response 0:
Let the required number of hours Ken must work the rest of the week be $x$.
For the first 10 hours, he earns $8 \cdot 10 = 80$ dollars. For the remaining  $x$ hours, he earns $10x$ dollars.
He saves $90 \%$ of his earnings, so we have that $0.90(80 + 10x) \geq 270$, which simplifies to $x \geq 22$. 
Therefore, the least number of hours Ken must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$270$ is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }22}$.
Response 1:
Let $x$ be the number of hours Ken has to work the rest of the week. If he works $x$ number of hours, he makes:
$$8\cdot10+(x)(10)=80+10x$$
Ken saves 90 percent of this amount, which is equal to:
$$0.9\cdot (80+10x) = 72+9x$$
To solve for $x$, we solve the inequality:
$$72+9x \geq 270$$
$$9x\geq198$$
$$x\geq22$$
This means the least number of hours Ken has to work the rest of the week is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }22}$ hours.

The y-intercept of the function should be the initial production, which is 4. Therefore, the function that models the production is:
$f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $f(x)$ \\\hline1 & 5 \\\hline3 & 13 \\\hline5 & 21 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of the linear function $f$ are shown in the table above. Which of the following defines $f$ ?

  C: $f(x)=4 x+1$
  D: $f(x)=5 x$

Slope $m$ is given by: $$m=\frac{f(x_2)-f(x_1)}{x_2-x_1}=\frac{21-5}{5-1}=4$$

So, the slope of $f$ is 4. We can check that only $(C)$ defines a linear function with a slope of 4: $$f(x)=(4)x+1$$

Therefore, the answer is: Answer("C").
Response 1:

This means that the slope of the function is $4$. To verify this, we can calculate the slope between any two points in the table, for example the first and second row: 

$$\text{slope}=\frac{\text{rise}}{\text{run}}=\frac{13-5}{3-1}=4 $$

Therefore, we know that $f(x)$ has a slope of $4$, and we can find the vertical intercept by checking one of the points in the table, for example, when $x=1$, then $f(1)=5$. This gives us the point $(1,5)$, and using the slope-intercept form of a line, we can find the equation of the function:

$$ f(x)=\text{slope}\cdot x + \text{vertical intercept}= 4x + 1 $$

Therefore, the answer is  $\boxed{\mathrm{(C)}\  f(x)=4 x+1}$.
Response 2:

We can use the coordinates (1,5) and (3,13) to find the slope.
$$m = \frac{13-5}{3-1} = 4$$

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& y<-x+a \\& y>x+b\end{aligned}$$In the $x y$-plane, if $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system of inequalities above, which of the following relationships between $a$ and $b$ must be true?
Choices:
  A: $a>b$
  B: $b>a$
  C: $|a|>|b|$
  D: $a=-b$
Response 0:
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Firstly, we should plot the two lines $y=-x+a$ and $y=x+b$. Since $y<x+b$ (line 2) is always greater than $y<-x+a$ (line 1) in the first quadrant, the area of interest is in the third quadrant: . 

We see that the lines $y=-x+a$ and $y=x+b$ pass through the point (-a, a) and (b, -b), respectively. Since $(0,0)$ is a solution, we have $a>0$ and $b<0$.

At the point $(0,0)$, the inequality $y<-x+a$ is always satisfied. Therefore, $y>x+b$ must be true. 

Solving $y > x+b$ simultaneously with the line $y=-x+a$, we get
\begin{align*}
-x+a &> x+b \\
\Rightarrow \quad a+b &> 0.
\end{align*}

Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(B) } b>a}$

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:
Let's start by finding out the amount charged by the electrician for Mr. Roland's job when he worked $h$ hours. We can plug in $h$ into the given equation and get:
$$C_R = 75h + 125$$
For Ms. Sanchez's job, we know that the electrician worked 2 hours more. So, the number of hours worked for Ms. Sanchez's job can be expressed as $(h+2)$. Therefore, the amount charged by the electrician for Ms. Sanchez's job can be expressed as:
$$C_S = 75(h+2) + 125 = 75h + 175$$
To find out how much more Ms. Sanchez was charged than Mr. Roland, we need to subtract $C_R$ from $C_S$:
$$C_S - C_R = (75h+175) - (75h+125)= 50$$
Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$50$ more than Mr. Roland.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
To solve this problem, we'll need to substitute $h+2$ for $h$ in the equation $C = 75h + 125$, since the electrician worked two hours longer at Ms. Sanchez's job than at Mr. Roland's job. 

For Mr. Roland's job, we get: 

$$C = 75h + 125$$
$$C = 75(h) + 125$$
$$C = 75h + 125$$

For Ms. Sanchez's job, we get: 

$$C = 75(h+2) + 125$$
$$C = 75h + 150 + 125$$
$$C = 75h + 275$$

So, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $75h + 275$ dollars, and charged Mr. Roland $75h + 125$ dollars. To find the difference, we need to subtract the amount Mr. Roland was charged from the amount Ms. Sanchez charged: 

$$(75h + 275) - (75h + 125) = 150$$

Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$150$ more than he charged Mr. Roland.

$$C_1 = 75x+125$$

$$C_2 = 75(x+2)+125$$

$$C_2-C_1 = 75(x+2)+125-(75x+125) = 75x+150-75x = 150$$

Therefore, the answer is $150$.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 58 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Energy per Gram of Typical Macronutrients.\begin{center}.\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}.\hline.Macronutrient & Food calories & Kilojoules \\.\hline.Protein & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.Fat & 9.0 & 37.7 \\.\hline.Carbohydrate & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.\end{tabular}.\end{center}.The table above gives the typical amounts of energy per gram, expressed in both food calories and kilojoules, of the three macronutrients in food.
Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
The amount of energy from $p$ grams of protein is $4p$ food calories, the amount from $f$ grams of fat is $9f$ food calories, and the amount from $c$ grams of carbohydrate is $4c$ food calories. We set the sum equal to 180 and solve for $f$: \begin{align*}
4p+9f+4c&=180\text{ food calories} \\
9f&=180-4p-4c \\
f&=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)
\end{align*} Answer: \boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)}
Response 1:

$$4p+9f+4c=180$$
Simplifying the above equation, we get:
$$9f=180-4p-4c=176-4(p+c)=4(44-(p+c))$$
$$f=\frac{4}{9}(44-(p+c))+20=\frac{4}{9}(20+(p+c))$$

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 60 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40 \\.& D(P)=220-P.\end{aligned}.$$.The quantity of a product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are functions of the price of the product. The functions above are the estimated supply and demand functions for a certain product. The function $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars, and the function $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Question: At what price will the quantity of the product supplied to the market equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 90$
  B: $\$ 120$
  C: $\$ 133$
  D: $\$ 155$
Response 0:
To find the price at which the quantity of the product supplied equals the quantity demanded, we need to solve for $P$ in the equation $$S(P) = D(P).$$ We can substitute the expressions for $S(P)$ and $D(P)$ given in the problem and solve for $P$: $$\begin{aligned} S(P) & = D(P) \\ \frac{1}{2} P+40 & = 220-P \\ \frac{3}{2} P & = 180 \\ P & = 120. \end{aligned}$$ Therefore, the answer is $\$ 120$. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
To find the equilibrium price, we need to find the price $P$ where $S(P) = D(P)$. Substituting the given functions, we have: 

$$\frac{1}{2} P+40 = 220 - P$$

Simplifying:

  D: $\frac{1}{2}$

Solution:

\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{x}&=\frac{15}{x+20} \\

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 64 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$2 a x-15=3(x+5)+5(x-1)$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, what is the value of $a$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 2
  C: 4
  D: 8
Response 0:
First, we can simplify the right-hand side of the equation by combining like terms: 

$$2ax - 15 = 3x + 15 - 5 + 5x$$
$$2ax - 15 = 7x + 10$$
$$2ax = 7x + 25$$
$$x=\frac{7}{2a}+\frac{25}{2a}.$$

Since we are told that no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, that means the expression on the right-hand side (which simplifies to $7x + 25$) can never equal the expression on the left-hand side (which is $2ax - 15$). In other words, the coefficient of $x$ on the right-hand side (which is 7) must be different from the coefficient of $x$ on the left-hand side (which is $2a$).

So we solve the equation $2a \neq 7$:

$$ 2a \neq 7 $$
$$ a \neq \frac{7}{2} $$

Therefore, the value of $a$ that would make no value of $x$ satisfy the equation is $a=\frac{7}{2}$.

Action: Answer("None of the Above")

\end{align*}

\begin{align*}

x(2a-8) &= 25 \\
x &= \frac{25}{2a-8}
\end{align*}

Since no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, it follows that the denominator of $x$ must be equal to 0. Therefore, we must have $2a-8 = 0$, which gives us $a=4$.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 67 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The function $f$ is defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$. The graph of $f$ in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following intervals contains the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-4<x<-3$
  B: $-3<x<1$
  C: $1<x<3$
  D: $3<x<4$
Response 0:
Action: Answer("-2")  

Explanation:

We can expand the given equation for the function $f$ as:
$$f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)=x^2+4x+3.$$
We can see that the coefficient of $x^2$ is positive, which means that the parabola opens upwards. 
The $x$-coordinate of the vertex of this parabola is given by the formula $x=-\dfrac{b}{2a}$, where $a$ is the coefficient of $x^2$ and $b$ is the coefficient of $x$. In this case, $a=1$ and $b=4$, so
$$x=-\dfrac{4}{2(1)}=-2.$$ 
Therefore, the correct answer is -2. The interval that contains $-2$ is the interval $-3<x<1$, which is choice $\textbf{(B)}$.
Response 1:
Action: Answer("-2") 

To find the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of a quadratic function defined by $f(x)=a x^{2}+b x+c$,
we can use the formula $x=- \frac{b}{2 a}$. In this problem, 
\begin{align*}
f(x) &= (x+3)(x+1) \\
&= x^{2} + 4 x + 3 \\
&= (x^{2} + 4 x + 4) - 1 \\
&= (x+2)^{2} -1
\end{align*}
Therefore, the vertex of the graph of $y=f(x)$ is $(-2,-1)$. 
The interval that contains $-2$ is $-3 < x < 1$, which is choice $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}}$.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 68 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\frac{2}{3}(9 x-6)-4=9 x-6$$Based on the equation above, what is the value of $3 x-2$ ?
Choices:
  A: -4
  B: $-\frac{4}{5}$
  C: $-\frac{2}{3}$
  D: 4
Response 0:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Action: Answer("D")  

Solution:

$$ \begin{aligned} \frac{2}{3}(9 x-6)-4 &=9 x-6 \\ (6x - 4) - 4 &= 9x - 6 \\ 6x - 8 &= 9x - 6 \\ -8 + 6 &= 9x - 6x \\ -2 &= 3x \\ \frac{-2}{3} &= x \\ \end{aligned} $$

Substitute the value of $x$ in $3x - 2$ :

$$ 3\left(\frac{-2}{3} \right) -2 = -6/3 -2 = -2 -2 = -4 $$

Hence, the answer is 4 (option D).
Response 2:
Action: Answer("D")  
Solution:

Choices:
  A: 1.2
  B: 15
  C: 48
  D: 72
Response 0:
To answer the question, we need to find 15% of 8 hours which is: 

$0.15 \times 8$ hours $ = 1.2 $ hours

Then, we can convert 1.2 hours to minutes by multiplying with 60:

$1.2 \times 60$ minutes $ = 72$ minutes

Therefore, Action: Answer("D") is the correct answer.

Since there are 60 minutes in an hour, we can convert hours to minutes by multiplying by 60:

$1.2 \text{ hours} \cdot 60\frac{\text{minutes}}{\text{hour}}= 72 \text{ minutes}$

Therefore, Lani spent 72 minutes of her workday in meetings.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 79 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $(a x+2)(b x+7)=15 x^{2}+c x+14$ for all values of $x$, and $a+b=8$, what are the two possible values for $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3 and 5
  B: 6 and 35
  C: 10 and 21
  D: 31 and 41
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
We can begin by expanding the left-hand side, which will give us:
$$abx^{2}+(7a+2b)x+14=15x^{2}+cx+14$$
Now we can equate the coefficients of $x^{2}$, $x$, and the constant term, to get the following system of equations:
\begin{align*}
ab &= 15 \\
7a + 2b &= c \\
14 &= 14
\end{align*}
We can solve for $a$ and $b$ by substituting $b=8-a$ into the first equation, giving us $a(8-a)=15$, which can be simplified to $a^{2}-8a+15=(a-5)(a-3)=0$. So $a=5$ or $a=3$, which gives us $b=3$ or $b=5$ respectively. Now we can substitute these values of $a$ and $b$ into the second equation to get $c=7a+2b=37$ or $c=7a+2b=17$ respectively. Therefore, the two possible values for $c$ are 17 and 37, which is option:

Answer("D")
Response 3:
Action: Answer("B")
Response 4:
Solution: We can first distribute the left-hand side of the equation to get \begin{align*}
(ab)x^2+(7a+2b)x+14 &= 15x^2 + cx + 14 \\
\Rightarrow \qquad (ab - 15)x^2 + (7a + 2b - c)x &= 0.
\end{align*} For this to hold for all values of $x$, both terms inside the parentheses must equal zero. Since we cannot have $ab = 15$ (otherwise the polynomial would be higher degree), we know that $7a+2b = c$. We also know that $a+b = 8$, so $b = 8-a$. Substituting this into the equation for $c$, we have $c = 7a + 2(8-a) = 6a+16$. Thus, the possible values of $c$ are the values that can be obtained by plugging in integer values from $0$ to $6$ for $a$. This gives us $c = 16, 22, 28, 34, 40, 46$. The answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A) } 3 \text{ and } 5}$.
Response 5:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 6:
Action: Answer("B")
Response 7:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 8:
Solution:

First, we expand the left-hand side of the equation:
$$
(a x+2)(b x+7)=a b x^{2}+(7 a+2 b) x+14
$$
So $a b=15$ and $7 a+2 b=c$.

We know that $a+b=8$, so $b=8-a$, which we can substitute into the equation $a b=15$ to get:
\begin{align*}
a(8-a) &= 15 \\
8a-a^2 &= 15 \\
a^2 - 8a + 15 &= 0\\
(a-3)(a-5)&=0\\
a&=3,5
\end{align*}

Now, we can substitute these values into $7a+2b=c$ to get the possible values of $c$:
\begin{align*}

a=5, b=3: & \quad 7(5)+2(3)=\boxed{\textbf{(C) }21}

The table shows the amount, in dollars, the company paid for each property and the corresponding monthly rental price, in dollars, the company charges for the property at each of the five locations. 23The relationship between the monthly rental price $r$, in dollars, and the property's purchase price $p$, in thousands of dollars, can be represented by a linear function. Which of the following functions represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $r(p)=2.5 p-870$
  B: $r(p)=5 p+165$
  C: $r(p)=6.5 p+440$
  D: $r(p)=7.5 p-10$
Response 0:
To solve the problem, we need to determine the slope-intercept form $r(p)=mp+b$ where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the $y$-intercept.

We notice that if we increase the purchase price of a property by 1,000 dollars then the corresponding rent increases by a certain amount. This shows us that there is a linear relationship between the rental price and the purchase price.

To get the slope, we can choose any two pairs $(p_1,r_1)$ and $(p_2,r_2)$ from the data and use the slope formula:

$$m=\frac{r_2-r_1}{p_2-p_1}$$

Let's use the pairs $(128, 950)$ and $(176, 1310)$:

$$m=\frac{1310-950}{176-128}=\frac{360}{48}=7.5$$

So the slope is 7.5. 

To get the y-intercept, we can use one of the points and solve for $b$. 
Using $(128,950)$,
$$950=7.5(128)+b$$
$$b=-10$$

Therefore, the function is:

$$r(p)=7.5 p-10$$

Action: Answer("D")

  C: 700 meters
  D: 1,400 meters

Distance walked in 240 seconds = 436.8 meters

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 87 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& b=2.35+0.25 x \\& c=1.75+0.40 x\end{aligned}$$In the equations above, $b$ and $c$ represent the price per pound, in dollars, of beef and chicken, respectively, $x$ weeks after July 1 during last summer. What was the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 2.60$
  B: $\$ 2.85$
  C: $\$ 2.95$
  D: $\$ 3.35$
Response 0:
To find the price per pound of beef when it was equal to the price per pound of chicken, we need to set $b=c$. So, we can solve the system of equations as follows: 

$$\begin{aligned}b&=c \\2.35+0.25x&=1.75+0.40x \\0.15x&=0.60 \\x&=4\end{aligned}$$

So, $x=4$ weeks after July 1. Now we can substitute this value of $x$ into either equation to find the price per pound of beef (which is the same as the price per pound of chicken at this time):

$$b=2.35+0.25(4)=\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ \\$2.95}$$

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ \\$2.95}$.
Response 1:
We need to find the value of $x$ when $b=c$. Using the given equations,

$$2.35+0.25x=1.75+0.40x$$

Simplifying, we get:

$$0.15x=0.60 \Rightarrow x=4$$

So, the prices are equal 4 weeks after July 1. We can find the price by substituting $x=4$ in either equation.

$$b=2.35 + 0.25\cdot 4 = \boxed{\$ 2.45}$$

Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(None of the Above)}}$ (The closest option is A, but 2.45 is slightly lower than 2.60)
Response 2:
When the price per pound of beef equals the price per pound of chicken,
$$b=c$$
Substituting the given expressions for $b$ and $c$ yields
$$2.35+0.25 x=1.75+0.40 x$$
Solving for $x$,
$$0.15 x=0.6\quad\implies\quad x=4$$

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 89 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Survey Results\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hlineRarely & $24.3 \%$ \\\hlineOften & $13.5 \%$ \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows the results of a survey in which tablet users were asked how often they would watch video advertisements in order to access streaming content for free. Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?
Choices:
  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69
Response 0:
Let's use the formula for conditional probability: $P(A|B)=\frac{P(A\cap B)}{P(B)}$, where $A$ is the event "answered 'Always'", and $B$ is the event "did not answer 'Never'".
We can find $P(B)$ as follows: $P(B)=1-P(Never)=1-0.313=0.687$
To find $P(Always\cap B)$, we want to know the proportion of people who answered "Always" out of those who did not answer "Never". So we have: $P(Always\cap B) = \frac{Always}{Rarely+Often+Always}=\frac{0.309}{0.243+0.135+0.309}\approx 0.38$
Putting it all together: $P(Always|B)=\frac{P(Always\cap B)}{P(B)}\approx\frac{0.38}{0.687}\approx0.55\approx \boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ 0.45}$
Response 1:
Let's assume there are 100 tablet users. According to the table, 31.3 of them never watch video ads to access streaming content for free. So, there are $100-31.3=68.7$ tablet users who are not "Never". Out of these $68.7$ tablet users,  $30.9 \%$ of them watch video ads "always". So, 

$30.9 \%$ of $68.7=21.22$

Thus, 21.22 tablet users watch video ads "always" but not "never". Therefore, the closest probability of a tablet user watching ads "always" given they are not watching "never" is:

$\frac{21.22}{68.7}\approx 0.308$, which is closest to $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\ 0.31}$. 

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Let $N$ be the event of answering "Never," and $A$ be the event of answering "Always." We want to calculate\[P(A|N^c)=\frac{P(A\cap N^c)}{P(N^c)}.\]We can calculate $P(N^c)$ by summing the percentages of answering "Rarely," "Often," and "Always," which is $0.243+0.135+0.309=0.687.$

Since we know each of these events is exclusive, we also have $P(A\cap N^c) = 0.309,$ so \[P(A|N^c) = \frac{0.309}{0.687} \approx 0.45.\]Thus, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) } 0.45}.$
Response 3:
Let $A$ represent the event that the survey response is "Always" and let $B$ represent the event that the survey response is not "Never". We want to find $P(A|B)$, which is:

$$P(A|B)=\frac{P(A \cap B)}{P(B)}$$

We can calculate $P(B)$ as $100\%$ minus the $31.3\%$ who responded "Never":

$$P(B)=100 \% - 31.3 \% = 68.7 \%$$

We're not given the probability of $A \cap B$ directly, but we can use Bayes' theorem to find it:

$$P(A \cap B)=P(B|A)\cdot P(A)=\frac{P(A|B)\cdot P(B)}{P(A|B)\cdot P(B)+P(A|\sim B)\cdot P(\sim B)}$$

where $\sim B$ represents the complement of $B$, i.e. the event that a user answered "Never." 

We know that $P(A)=30.9 \%$, $P(\sim B)=31.3 \% - 0.0 \% = 31.3 \%$, and $P(A|\sim B)=0 \%$ (by definition of conditional probability). Plugging in these values and solving for $P(A|B)$, we get:

$$P(A|B)=\frac{P(B|A)\cdot P(A)}{P(B|A)\cdot P(A)+P(\sim B|A)\cdot P(A|\sim B)}=\frac{(13.5 \%) \cdot (30.9 \%)}{(13.5 \%) \cdot (30.9 \%) + (0 \%)\cdot (31.3 \%)} \approx 0.38$$

Therefore, the answer is (B) $0.38$.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 5:
Let $N$, $R$, $O$, and $A$ represent the events that a person answered "Never", "Rarely", "Often", and "Always", respectively. We are interested in finding $P(A|C)$, where $C$ is the complement of $N$. We can use Bayes' Theorem to find this probability: $P(A|C) = \frac{P(C|A)P(A)}{P(C)}$. We know that $P(C|A) = (1 - 0.313 - 0.243 - 0.135) = 0.309$, since everyone must belong to one of these categories (never, rarely, often, or always). We also know that $P(A) = 0.309$, which is the percentage of people who answered "Always". To find $P(C)$, we can use the Law of Total Probability: $P(C) = P(C|N)P(N) + P(C|R)P(R) + P(C|O)P(O) + P(C|A)P(A)$. We know that $P(C|N) = 0$ (since "never" means they didn't watch any ads), $P(N) = 0.313$, $P(C|R) = 0.243/(1-0.313) \approx 0.354$, $P(R) = 0.243$, $P(C|O) = 0.135/(1-0.313) \approx 0.196$, and $P(O) = 0.135$. Plugging in these values, we get: $P(C) = 0 + 0.313 \cdot 0.354 + 0.243 \cdot 0.354 + 0.135 \cdot 0.309 \approx 0.28$. Therefore, $P(A|C) = \frac{0.309 \cdot 0.309}{0.28} \approx \boxed{\textbf{(B) } 0.38}$.

Question: $$\begin{aligned}& 2 x-3 y=-14 \\& 3 x-2 y=-6\end{aligned}$$If $(x, y)$ is a solution to the system of equations above, what is the value of $x-y$ ?
Choices:
  A: -20
  B: $\quad-8$
  C: -4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C") 

Here's the method to solve it:
From the first equation, we get $2x = 3y - 14$, which simplifies to $x = \frac{3}{2}y -7$. Substituting this value of $x$ into the second equation gives $3(\frac{3}{2}y - 7) - 2y = -6$. Simplifying that equation leads us to get $y=2$. Substituting the value of $y$ in $x = \frac{3}{2}y -7$, we get $x = -1$.

Hence, $x-y = -1-2= -3 \implies$ Answer is C (-4).
Response 1:
Action: Answer("B") 

We can solve the system of equations by using elimination. First, multiply the first equation by $(-2)$ and the second equation by $3$, and then add them up:

$$\begin{aligned} -4x+6y&=28\\ 9x-6y&=-18\\ \end{aligned} $$

Summing up both, we get:

$$5x=10\implies x=2$$

Substituting x=2 in either of the original equations, we get $y=4$. Therefore, $x-y=2-4=-2$. Thus, the answer is B) -8.
Response 2:
Action: Answer("D")

$$\begin{aligned} 4x-6y&=-28\\ 9x-6y&=-18\\ \hline -5x&=-10 \end{aligned}$$
So we have $x=2$. We can then substitute $x=2$ in either of the original equations to find $y$:
$$\begin{aligned} 2 (2)-3 y&=-14\\ y&=8\\ \end{aligned}$$
Finally, we can calculate $x-y$ as $2-8=-6$. Therefore, the answer is $\textbf{(B)}$ $-8$.

\end{align*}

\begin{align*}

\frac{9}{2}y-21-2y &= -6 \\
\frac{5}{2}y &= 15 \\
y &= 6
\end{align*}

\begin{align*}

2x-3(6) &=-14 \\
2x &= 16 \\
x &= 8
\end{align*}

Therefore, $(x,y) = (8,6)$, and $x-y=2$. The correct answer is (D).

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 92 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A line in the $x y$-plane passes through the origin and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Which of the following points lies on the line?
Choices:
  A: $(0,7)$
  B: $(1,7)$
  C: $(7,7)$
  D: $(14,2)$
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
We know that if a line passes through the origin $(0,0)$ and has a slope of $m$, the equation of the line is $y=mx$. Here, the slope of the line is $\frac{1}{7}$, so the equation of the line is $y=\frac{1}{7}x$. Let's substitute each point into this equation and see which one works:  
A: $(0,7) \Rightarrow 7 = \frac{1}{7}(0)$. This point does not lie on the line because $y \neq 0$.  
B: $(1,7) \Rightarrow 7 = \frac{1}{7}(1)$. This point does not lie on the line because the equation is satisfied only if $x=7$.  
C: $(7,7) \Rightarrow 7 = \frac{1}{7}(7)$. This point lies on the line.  
D: $(14,2) \Rightarrow 2 = \frac{1}{7}(14)$. This point does not lie on the line because the equation is satisfied only if $y=2$.  

Therefore, the point that lies on the line is $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ (7,7)}$.
Response 3:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
We can use the point-slope form of the equation of a line to solve this question. The point-slope form of a line with slope $m$ passing through the point $(x_1, y_1)$ is given by:

$y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)$

In this case, the line passes through the origin $(0,0)$ and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Therefore, the equation of the line is:

$y - 0 = \frac{1}{7}(x - 0)$

which simplifies to:

$y = \frac{1}{7}x$

Now we can plug in each of the answer choices and see which ones satisfy this equation:

(A) $(0,7)$:
$7 \neq \frac{1}{7}(0)$ (not on the line)

(B) $(1,7)$:
$7 \neq \frac{1}{7}(1)$ (not on the line)

(C) $(7,7)$:
$7 = \frac{1}{7}(7)$ (on the line)

(D) $(14,2)$:
$2 \neq \frac{1}{7}(14)$ (not on the line)

Therefore, the point that lies on the given line is (C) $(7,7)$.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 5:
Action: Answer("A")

Checking the first point, $(0,7)$, we get $y=\frac{1}{7}x = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 0 = 0 \neq 7$. Therefore, this point does not lie on the line.

Checking the second point, $(1,7)$, we get $y=\frac{1}{7}x = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 1 = \frac{1}{7} \neq 7$. Therefore, this point does not lie on the line.

Checking the third point, $(7,7)$, we get $y=\frac{1}{7}x = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 7 = 1 = 7$. Therefore, this point lies on the line.

Checking the fourth point, $(14,2)$, we get $y=\frac{1}{7}x = \frac{1}{7} \cdot 14 = 2 \neq 2$. Therefore, this point does not lie on the line.

Therefore, the point that lies on the line is $(7, 7)$.

$$C: (7,7) \rightarrow 7 = \frac{1}{7}(7)$$
$$D: (14,2) \rightarrow 2 \neq \frac{1}{7}(14)$$
Therefore, the point on the line is (B) $(1,7)$.

In addition, each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
Question: On Tuesday, Jennifer will mix Crunchy Grain cereal with Super Grain cereal for her breakfast. Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup. If the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, how much Super Grain cereal is in one cup of the mixture?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$
  C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$
  D: $\frac{1}{2} \operatorname{cup}$

$210\left(\frac{3}{4}\right) + 240x = 270$

Simplifying the equation gives us:

$157.5 + 240x = 270$

$240x = 112.5$

$x = \frac{112.5}{240} = \frac{3}{8}$

Therefore, Jennifer mixes $\frac{3}{8}$ cup Super Grain cereal with $\frac{5}{8}$ cup Crunchy Grain cereal.

Since we know that the total number of calories in one cup of the mixture is 270, we can set up the equation: 
$\frac{240x+280y}{x+y}=270$
Multiplying both sides by $x+y$, we get: 
$240x+280y=270(x+y)$
$240x+280y=270x+270y$
$10x=10y$
$x=y$
Therefore, Jennifer uses the same amount of Super Grain and Crunchy Grain cereal.

$1 = \frac{27}{26}x + \frac{3}{4}x$ 

$1 = \frac{135}{104}x$ 

$x = \frac{104}{135}$

So, the amount of Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture is $\frac{104}{135}$ cups, which is approximately $\frac{3}{8}$ cups.

\end{align*}

\Rightarrow\qquad x&=\frac{450}{960}=\frac{15}{32}
\end{align*}

\begin{align*}
\frac{3}{4}+\frac{15}{32} &= \frac{24}{32}+\frac{15}{32}\\
&= \frac{39}{32}.
\end{align*}
This makes sense, since the sum of two positive quantities is always larger than either quantity by itself. Thus, the amount of Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture is $\frac{15}{32}$, which simplifies to $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\frac{1}{3}\text{ cup}}$ when expressed in terms of cups.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$-2 x+3 y=6$$In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is perpendicular to the graph of the equation above?
Choices:
  A: $3 x+2 y=6$
  B: $3 x+4 y=6$
  C: $2 x+4 y=6$
  D: $2 x+6 y=3$
Response 0:
Recall that two lines are perpendicular if and only if the product of their slopes is $-1 .$ Solve the given equation for $y$ to get $y=\frac{2}{3} x+2 .$ The slope of this line is $\frac{2}{3} .$ The line with slope $-1 / \frac{2}{3}=-\frac{3}{2}$ is the line with slope $\frac{3}{2}$ $$\Rightarrow y=\frac{3}{2} x+b.$$ Substituting $(-2,2)$ gives $2=\frac{3}{2} \cdot(-2)+b \Rightarrow b=8 .$ Therefore, the equation of the line perpendicular to the given equation is $y=\frac{3}{2} x+8$ and $\boxed{\textbf{(D) } 2x+6y=3}$ is the equation of the line.
Response 1:
We can determine whether two equations are perpendicular by checking if the product of their slopes is $-1$. 

First, let's write the equation $-2x + 3y = 6$ in slope-intercept form by solving for $y$: 

$$3y = 2x + 6 \Rightarrow y = \frac{2}{3} x + 2$$

So the slope of the line represented by $-2x + 3y = 6$ is $\frac{2}{3}$. 

Now we can check which of the equations have slopes that are negative reciprocals of $\frac{2}{3}$: 

A: $3x + 2y = 6 \Rightarrow 2y = -3x + 6 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{3}{2}x + 3$. The slope is $-\frac{3}{2}$, which is the negative reciprocal of $\frac{2}{3}$. 

B: $3x + 4y = 6 \Rightarrow 4y = -3x + 6 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{3}{4}x + \frac{3}{4}$. The slope is $-\frac{3}{4}$, which is NOT the negative reciprocal of $\frac{2}{3}$.

C: $2x + 4y = 6 \Rightarrow 4y = -2x + 6 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{1}{2}x + \frac{3}{2}$. The slope is $-\frac{1}{2}$, which is NOT the negative reciprocal of $\frac{2}{3}$.

D: $2x + 6y = 3 \Rightarrow 6y = -2x + 3 \Rightarrow y = -\frac{1}{3}x + \frac{1}{2}$. The slope is $-\frac{1}{3}$, which is the negative reciprocal of $\frac{2}{3}$. 

Therefore, the answer is $\textbf{(D) }2x+6y=3$.

### Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$In the system of equations above, $k$ is a constant and $x$ and $y$ are variables. For what value of $k$ will the system of equations have no solution?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{12}{5}$
  B: $\frac{16}{7}$
  C: $-\frac{16}{7}$
  D: $-\frac{12}{5}$
Response 0:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 4:
Action: Answer("B")
Response 5:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 6:
Action: Answer("C")
Response 7:
We can solve the system of equations using any method we prefer. For example, using elimination,

$$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$

Multiplying the first equation by 4, we get:

$$\begin{aligned}& 4k x-12 y=16 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$

We can now eliminate $x$ by subtracting the second equation from the first:

$$4k x - 4 x - 12 y +5 y =16-7$$

Simplifying:

$$\begin{aligned}& (4k-4) x - 7 y = 9 \\& (4k-4) x = 7 y + 9\end{aligned}$$

If we divide the second equation by $(4k-4)$, we get:

$$x = \frac{7}{4k-4} y + \frac{9}{4k-4}$$

If $4k -4=0$, then we have $x$ expressed as a linear function of $y$ and the two equations represent two parallel lines. Therefore, there will be no solution.

Solving $4k-4=0$, we get $k = 1$.

Therefore, for $k=1$, the system of equations has no solution.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 8:
Action: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Action: Answer("A")  
Votes: D, A, C, D, B, D, C, A, D, A

Question: If $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$, what is the value of $\frac{b}{a} ?$
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4}$
  C: 2
  D: 4
Response 0:
Solution: 
Given, $\frac{2 a}{b} = \frac{1}{2}$
Multiplying both sides by $\frac{b}{2},$ we get
$a = \frac{b}{4}$
Dividing both sides by $a,$ we get
$\frac{b}{a} = 4$
Answer: Action: Answer("D")

Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
We can start by cross-multiplying the given equation, which gives $4a=b$. Therefore, $$\frac{b}{a} = \frac{4a}{a} = \boxed{\textbf{(D) }4}.$$
Response 3:
Multiply both sides of the equation $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$ by $\frac{b}{2}$ to get $a = \frac{b}{4}$. Therefore, $\frac{b}{a} = \frac{4}{1} = 4$.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 4:
Given $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$, we can solve for b/a as follows:
$$
\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}
$$
$$\implies 2a = \frac{b}{2} = \frac{b}{2}\cdot\frac{a}{a} = \frac{ab}{2a}$$
$$\implies 4a^2 = b a$$
$$\implies \frac{b}{a} = 4$$

Therefore, the answer is (D) $4$. 

(Action: Answer("D"))

Response 7:
We can solve for $\frac{b}{a}$ by manipulating the given equation $\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$:
$$\frac{2a}{b}=\frac{1}{2} \qquad \Rightarrow \qquad 4a=b \qquad \Rightarrow \qquad \frac{b}{a}=\frac{4a}{a}=4$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}\ 4}$.
Response 8:
Solution: 

We can start this problem by solving for one of the variables in terms of the other using the given equation. 

$\frac{2 a}{b}=\frac{1}{2}$ 

Multiplying both sides by $b,$ we get 

$2a = \frac{b}{2}$ 

Or $b= 4a.$ 

So, 

$\frac{b}{a} = \frac{4a}{a} =4.$ 


Answer: $\boxed{\text{(D)}\ 4}$
